25/06/2025, 4:15â€¯pm - +91 94194 10786: Hello everyone,

I wanted to take a moment, explicitly before any campaigning begins, to share my thoughts about Chetan, someone I've had the pleasure of working closely with. To be clear, this message is *not a part of any campaign*, and I deliberately chose to send it before campaigning officially starts, after which I will refrain from sending any message over this groip.

I clearly recall when I first witnessed Chetan's dedication. It was during my tenure as a TA and our official TA sessions ended a week before the end term exams, yet someone continued voluntarily taking doubt sessions, often longer and more diligently than we did ourselves. That person was Chetan. After seeing his genuine commitment, I personally approached him to join the Paradox team, when I was the head of Sports department.

Throughout our journey in Paradox, his hardwork and reliability were remarkable. I've seen him tirelessly lead meetings, patiently assist event heads, and consistently go above and beyond, often ignoring my advice to ease up on himself. I clearly remember him taking meets which lasted literally over 8 hours, doing someone else's work just because they found it overwhelming. It was evident that his potential was more than just event management and for that particular reason, I placed him in the Student Relations team. He diligently handled issues, replied to mails which were pending from even Paradix'23 and later recruited some amazing people who later took on prominent roles not only within Paradox but also in UHC.

I haven't had the opportunity to work closely with the other candidates, and I hold equal respect for each of their contributions. My intention here is purely to present a side of Chetan, his dedication, and sincere effort, qualities I deeply admire, and which I feel deserve recognition regardless of election outcomes.

I understand some might question whether his contributions have been specifically for our house or primarily within Paradox. However, I genuinely believe that whether through UHC or Paradox, our ultimate goal remains serving the student community. 

My only wish for these elections is fairness, ethical conduct, and constructive discussions. Whether Chetan wins or loses, I believe itâ€™s important to acknowledge and highlight this side of him, which not a lot of people know. Do I see him achieving great things for the house? Absolutely, but my respect extends equally to every candidate participating.

May the most deserving and ethical candidate lead the house.

ğŸŒ¿ The Heart-Touching Journey of Srila Prabhupada

Born in 1896 in Kolkata (then Calcutta), Abhay Charanaravinda Bhaktivedanta Swami Prabhupada lived an ordinary life on the surface â€” a pharmacist, husband, and father. But deep within, his soul was burning with the divine instructions of his spiritual master, Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Sarasvati Thakur, who told him:

> "Preach Krishna consciousness in the English language to the Western world."



For decades, this instruction echoed in his heart, and though life presented him with many obstacles â€” family responsibilities, poverty, aging health â€” his spirit remained unshaken.


---

ğŸš¢ Crossing the Ocean at 69: A Journey of Pain and Faith

At the age of 69, when most people retire, Prabhupada boarded the cargo ship Jaladuta, bound for the United States. He had:

No money (just a few rupees)

No contacts

No institution or followers


He suffered two heart attacks during the voyage, nearly dying alone in the vast Atlantic. But Krishna was with him.

> In his diary, he wrote:
"O Lord Krishna, I have no power, but if You like, You can make my success possible."




---

ğŸŒ Planting the Seed of Bhakti in the West

Landing in New York in 1965, he lived in humble conditions â€” small rooms, park benches, even the homes of strangers. Slowly, he started chanting and speaking in Tompkins Square Park. The Western youth, lost in drugs and spiritual confusion, were drawn to his purity and compassion.

In 1966, he founded ISKCON (International Society for Krishna Consciousness), and a revolution in spiritual consciousness began.


---

ğŸ”¥ The Sacrifice of a Saint

Prabhupadaâ€™s journey was full of:

Sleepless nights

Writing books by candlelight (he translated 70+ volumes of sacred texts)

Constant travel (over 14 times around the globe in just 12 years!)

Facing opposition, criticism, and health challenges


Yet, he remained calm, always chanting Krishnaâ€™s name, always teaching with love and wisdom.


---

ğŸŒ¸ A Legacy of Love

By the time of his passing in 1977 in Vrindavan, Prabhupada had:

Established 108 temples worldwide

Inspired millions of people

Distributed millions of books

Created a global family of devotees


His mission was not about converting people, but awakening their love for God.


---

ğŸ•Šï¸ Conclusion: A Beacon for the Material World

Srila Prabhupada's journey shows how one pure soul, fully surrendered to God, can transform the world. His pain, sacrifice, and unshakable devotion were all for the spiritual upliftment of humanity â€” especially those lost in materialism.

He once said:

> "I have come here not to take anything, but to give â€” Krishna consciousness."

once matched, you'd get each otherâ€™s contact details (usually whatsapp) and could decide how you wanna collaborate - some just exchanged notes, some did weekly study calls, some even pulled all-nighters together before exams ğŸ˜‚

27/06/2025, 1:30â€¯pm - +91 77000 59796: The companionship program in *kaziranga* was a peer-based support thing we ran earlier.
we used to collect course info from everyone via a form, then match people who were doing the same subjects.
once matched, you'd get each otherâ€™s contact details (usually whatsapp) and could decide how you wanna collaborate - some just exchanged notes, some did weekly study calls, some even pulled all-nighters together before exams ğŸ˜‚
we had around 140+ students signed up last time - foundation, diploma, degree, everyone.
main idea was to make studying less isolating and build that sense of teamwork.
it paused for a while but thinking of reviving it now.
